APPENDIX I
RESEARCH DESIGN
The methods to be employed generally follow the Scope of Work for this
project, which has been prepared by Terry L. McClung, United States Forest
Service (USFS) Archeologist. Other details have been added by Brazos Valley
Research Associates (BVRA).
Pre-requisites for Archaeological Survey in the
Bienville National Forest
A Research Design and vitae of the Principal Investigator (William E.
Moore) and Project Archaeologist (Edward P. Baxter) will be submitted to the
USFS for approval. No work will be performed on land owned by the USFS until
the Research Design submitted by BVRA has been approved by the USFS, and
a Federal permit under the Archaeological Resources Protection Act (ARPA) has
been issued.
In accordance with Section 106 of the National Historic Preservation Act, a
Research Design and vitae of the Principal Investigator and Project
Archaeologist will be submitted to the State Historic Preservation Officer (SHPO)
for approval. No work will be performed on land owned by the USFS until
authorization in writing has been given by the SHPO.
Restrictions on Vehicular Traffic
No vehicles owned and/or operated by the archaeological personnel
working with BVRA will be driven across site boundaries, significant or not
significant. They will remain on roads maintained by the USFS.
All vehicle and equipment activity will be restricted to existing maintained
roads, old logging roads, skidder trails with old rutting scars, fire lanes, and
approved access routes. These will be marked with plastic flagging by hired
foresters for equipment travel prior to the field survey. Wheeled or tracked
vehicles and equipment, including All Terrain Vehicles, are permitted to cross
boundaries of known significant archaeological sites as long as no visible
damage is done such as rutting and/or broken ground.

1

General Field Methods
When archaeological sites are discovered in the project area during this
archaeological project, they will be flagged to make it easier for other
archaeologists to return for site delineation. Site significance recommendations
will be made by the Project Archaeologist, the Regional Specialist, and the
Principal Investigator based on a list of criteria provided by the USFS and
recommendations regarding site avoidance and/or protection will be presented in
the report. The final decision regarding site significance will be determined by
the USFS and/or the SHPO.
Shovel tests will be excavated by hand and will terminate when the clay
subsoil is reached. All dirt will be passed through ¼ inch hardware cloth.
Artifacts will be recorded by shovel test only. No attempt will be made to record
artifacts by level or depth.
Archaeological sites that have been determined by the USFS or SHPO
prior to this project to be not significant will not be visited or evaluated. This
information will be obtained from a database on file at the office of the SHPO and
records maintained by the USFS. Archaeological sites that have been
determined by the USFS or the SHPO prior to this project to be significant will be
avoided per the Scope of Work prepared by the USFS for work in the Bienville
National Forest.
Areas to be Shovel Tested
Shovel tests will be excavated at the proposed location of all source holes
and along access routes where soil movement such as rutting is expected to
occur. Shovel tests will only be excavated in areas where the slope is less than
15 degrees. One or more shovel tests will be dug at or very near the location of
the proposed source hole.
If the proposed source hole location is greater than 150 meters from a
known source of water, only one shovel test will be excavated unless the test
yields artifacts. Then, additional tests will be necessary to delineate the site.
In an area where the proposed source hole is located within 150 meters
from a permanent water source, one shovel test will be dug at the proposed
source hole location, and two additional shovel tests will be dug 15 meters from
the source hole in two different locations. The direction of these additional tests
will be determined in the field. If no site is found, only three shovel tests will be
excavated.

2

Shovel tests must be dug approximately every 30 meters along all new
routes that are suspected to undergo rutting and are on a slope of less than 15
degrees. The archaeologists, aided by the surveyors, will determine degree of
slope in the field. Efforts will be made to deviate from the 30-meter interval in
order to shovel test high probability areas such as the highest spot on a knoll or
levee ridge crest when new access routes cross these areas.
Areas that have been previously surveyed will not be shovel tested during
this project. These areas will be identified by plotting on the topographic maps at
the office of the SHPO and records maintained by the USFS.
Site Recording Procedures
When artifacts are found in a shovel test, additional shovel tests will be
excavated at five meter intervals from the discovery test until two consecutive
negative shovel tests occur. These tests will be dug in the four cardinal
directions approximately 90 degrees apart. Ten-meter intervals will be employed
on larger sites that are over 40 meters in length.
When an artifact is located in a shovel test, the shovel test interval will be
reduced to five meters in the four cardinal directions (90 degrees apart) from the
first positive shovel test. Ten meter intervals will be employed on larger sites that
are over 40 meters in length. No tests will be excavated in those directions
where the slope is greater than 15 degrees. These tests will continue until two
consecutive negative shovel tests occur in one of the directions.
The boundaries of all archaeological sites found during this survey will be
flagged with brightly colored plastic flagging tape tied to trees and shrubs.
The boundaries of all sites within the project area that have been
determined by the USFS or SHPO to be significant will be flagged for avoidance
during the project.
Site Avoidance
The seismic crew will avoid all previously recorded sites classified as
unknown or eligible for listing in the National Register of Historic Places by the
SHPO and/or USFS. The seismic crew will also avoid all newly recorded sites
found during this survey on lands managed by the USFS. A 50-meter buffer
zone will be placed around the boundaries of these sites. The field
archaeologists will shovel test alternative source hole locations that have been
moved out of the buffer zone. On a case-by-case basis, portions of potentially
eligible sites may be available for access or drilling if approved by the USFS
archaeologist.

3

Artifact Analysis
The Regional Specialist familiar with the area will analyze all artifacts
recovered during this project. The level of analysis will be consistent with prior
work in the Bienville National Forest. The Regional Specialist will process and
analyze all artifacts when site delineation and recordation is complete. The
formal analysis discussion will be presented in the final report.
Report Preparation
The results of the field survey will be documented in a comprehensive
report that will be submitted to the USFS and SHPO following the completion of
this survey. This report will not be considered final until it has met the guidelines
of both agencies.
•

The final report will accurately describe the methods followed during this
survey, the results of the survey, and recommendations for site testing
and/or avoidance.

•

The final report will contain drafted illustrations or photographs of selected
diagnostic artifacts.

•

The final report will contain maps of all archaeological sites recorded
during this survey at a sufficient scale to allow surface features and
locations of shovel tests dug within the site and those used to delineate
the site.

•

Copies of site cards and other bulky data such as field notes will be
presented in a separate volume for permanent curation. These data will
be summarized in the report.
Artifact Curation

All artifacts collected during this project will be housed at the office of the
Regional Specialist until the survey is completed and the report has been written
and submitted for review. At that time, the artifacts will be submitted to the
USFS. The USFS will be responsible for their protection and eventual
submission to the Cobb Institute if necessary. Certain specimens collected
during shovel testing may be determined to be not cultural. The Regional
Specialist will recommend in writing to the USFS archaeologist that they be
discarded. No artifacts will be removed from the inventory without permission of
the USFS archaeologist.

4

Avoidance Plan
The project area will be divided into five sections, each containing
approximately 20 percent of the area. When the field survey of each area is
complete (all the source points and access routes have been investigated and
newly discovered sites delineated and recorded), an avoidance plan will be
submitted to the USFS archaeologist. This plan will list the previously recorded
significant sites by state trinomial or USFS field identification numbers, and all
newly recorded sites will be listed by state trinomials or field identification
numbers. A statement of site avoidance procedures will accompany the list.
Maps depicting the location of all sites to be avoided will be made available to the
USFS archaeologist and the seismic operators by DESCO. Upon submittal and
approval of this avoidance plan, the USFS archaeologist will grant drilling
privileges for the 20 percent section.
The archaeological crew will continue the field survey in the next 20
percent area. All data from the first 20 percent area will continue to be
processed and transmitted to those persons working on the report such as the
Regional Specialist, Draftsperson, and Principal Investigator. Bi-weekly progress
reports will be submitted to the USFS archaeologist by the Principal Investigator
to insure report preparation activity schedules are being maintained.
Archaeological Investigations Supporting Drilling Activity
During the course of the drilling activities, some established source point
locations and some access route locations may have to be changed. When this
situation arises, an archaeologist will accompany the surveyor(s) and/or forester
who will make the necessary changes. The archaeologist will shovel test the
new source point location and/or access route as stated in the Research Design.
If a site is found, the source point and/or access route will be moved again and
re-investigated. The site will be delineated and recorded and buffered as stated
above. Reports of these activities will be incorporated into the final report.

5

APPENDIX IV
PREVIOUS INVESTIGATIONS
IN THE BIENVILLE NATIONAL FOREST
1989
Lauro, James T.
1989a Untitled letter report submitted to the Farmers Home
Administration. (89-010)*
A survey of an 81.5-acre tract was conducted by archaeologist James T. Lauro of
Archaeology Mississippi. No archaeological sites were found.
Lauro, James T.
1989b Untitled letter report submitted to the Farmers Home
Administration. (89-217)
A survey of a two-acre tract was conducted by archaeologist James T. Lauro of
Archaeology Mississippi. No archaeological sites were found.
Scott, Susan L.
1989 Cultural Resource Survey of Proposed Oilwell Site in Smith County,
Mississippi, North Central Oil Corporation Houston, Texas.
Unnumbered letter report prepared by Scott and Associates,
Hattiesburg, Mississippi. (89-195)
Survey of well site adjacent to 22-Sm-510, which is located in the project area.
No evidence of this site was found, and no new sites were recorded.
1991
Lauro, James T.
1991 Cultural Resources Survey 3 to 4 Acre Parcel of Land Smith
County, Mississippi. Unnumbered letter report submitted to Wallace
Ray Sanderford by James T. Lauro of Archaeology Mississippi. (91147)
No sites were found.

1

1992
Lauro, James
1992 Cultural Resources Survey of 2 Proposed Borrow Pits, Smith
County, Mississippi. Unnumbered report prepared by Archaeology
Mississippi. (92-320)
An archaeological survey was conducted at the location of two proposed borrow
pits (2 acres and 3 acres) by James Lauro. No archaeological sites or standing
structures were found.
Reams, Melissa H.
1992a Future Sale Areas, Strong River Ranger District, Bienville National
Forest: Scott, Smith and Jasper Counties. United States
Department of Agriculture Forest Service Cultural Resource
Inventory Report Series 92-08-07-10-01. (92-164)
An archaeological survey of 901 acres of future sale areas was conducted in May
1992 by Bienville National Forest Archeologist Melissa Reams. Three new sites
and one isolated find were found. Two sites are in the project area. They are
22-Sm-522 and 22-Sm-523. Not one of these sites is eligible for listing in the
National Register of Historic Places. The isolated find consisting of three chert
flakes (RA-247-IF-1) also appears to be in the project area.
Reams, Melissa H.
1992b 1992 Compartment Prescriptions – Part II, Strong River Ranger
District, Bienville National Forest: Scott, Smith, and Jasper
Counties, Mississippi. United States Department of Agriculture
Forest Service Cultural Resource Inventory Report Series 92-0807-10-03. (92-227)
An archaeological survey of two 1992 compartment prescription areas (970
acres) was conducted in June1992 by Bienville National Forest Archeologist
Melissa Reams. The McLaurin Cemetery and one isolated find – a soda water
bottle probably manufactured prior to 1920 (242-IF-1) were found in
Compartment 242.
Ecology and Environment, Inc.
1992 Mississippi Cultural Resource Surveys for the Tennessee Gas
Pipeline Company West-East Crossover Project Docket No. CP911627-000. Prepared for Tennessee Gas Pipeline Company by
Ecology and Environment, Inc., Houston.
An archaeological survey of a gas pipeline recorded one prehistoric site (22-SM518) in the project area

2

1993
Lauro, James T.
1993 Cultural Resources Survey of 2 Proposed Oil Wells Smith County,
Mississippi. Untitled letter report submitted Norcen Explorer, Inc.
(93-224)
An archaeological survey of two proposed well sites in Smith County, Mississippi
was performed by archaeologist James Lauro in 1993. No sites were found.
Reams, Melissa H.

mechanical work in May of 1995. In all, 446 shovel tests were excavated. Thirtynine previously unrecorded sites were identified, and four previously recorded
sites were assessed. Not one of these sites is eligible for listing in the National

McClung, Terry L.
1996a A Heritage Resource Inventory of Timber Stands Selected for
Mechanical Site Preparation, Bienville National Forest, Jasper and
Smith Counties, Mississippi. Heritage Resource Inventory Report
Series 96-08-07-BV-09 (96-215)
An archaeological survey within 12 timber stands was conducted in July of 1996
by Terry L. McClung, archaeologist for the Bienville National Forest. Seven
prehistoric sites, 4 historic sites, and 3 sites with prehistoric components were
recorded. All of these sites have undergone various amounts of damage by early
farming and modern timber management practices. Not one of these sites is
eligible for listing in the National Register of Historic Places. Those in the current
project area are 22-Sm-550, 22-Sm-551, and 22-Sm-705.
McClung, Terry L.

Compartment 246, Stands 1,2, 4, 5, and 8 in Bienville National

Report Series 96-08-07-BV-10 (96-221)
An archaeological survey at five adjoining stands of timber in Compartment 246
of the Bienville National Forest was conducted in July of 1996 by Forest Service
archaeologist, Terry L. McClung. Six previously unrecorded sites in the current
project area (22-Sm-697 – 22-Sm-701) and one isolated find (96-246-BV-10)
were found. Not one of these sites is eligible for listing in the National Register of
Historic Places.

APPENDIX IX
GUIDELINES FOR SITE SIGNIFICANCE
These guidelines are offered to private contractors and new Forest
Service archaeologists as a guide to determine site significance during a survey
using shovel testing. By the term “significant,” we are referring to Class I and
Class II sites. Beyond these guidelines, a great deal of discretion is given to the
researcher with the assumption that they are familiar with the basic tenets of
archaeology within the state.
•

Class I sites are those that are already listed on the National Register of
Historic Places (NRHP) or are eligible for listing on the NHRP.

•

Class II sites are those that may have the potential for listing on the
NRHP.

•

Class III sites are those that are not eligible for listing on the NRHP.
SIGNIFICANCE CRITERIA

(a) The number of significant prehistoric sites should contain a representative
sample of site types encountered during the survey. This includes small,
medium, and larges sites that only produce a few flakes (lithic scatters). This
also includes a sample of sites found on various land forms such as the end of a
low toe ridge, a knoll on a parent ridge, or the end of a high ridge, etc. The main
reason for this sampling is that past excavations have shown that shovel testing
gives us very little indication of what cultures are truly present at a site.
(b) A sample of historic sites that produce predominantly pearlware sherds (or
other pre-1840 Euro-American sherd types). Not more than 50 percent of these
sites should be considered as significant.
(c) You should favor prehistoric sites that have all of the three soil strata (A, E,
and B soils). These soils are an indication that little erosion has taken place in
the past. However, many significant sites may contain no A soil horizon.
(d) Any prehistoric sites that are shown to have a buried A horizon.
(e) Any sites that produce cultural debris unusually deeper than the other sites
discovered.
(f) Any lithic quarry site
g) Any site that produced prismatic blade(s) or bladelet(s)

1

(h) Any prehistoric site that contains an animal or human burial or burials
(i) Any prehistoric site that contains an artifact cache
(j) Any prehistoric site that may indicate specific activity areas are present.
(k) Any prehistoric site that contains (or appears to contain) an artificial earthwork
(l) Any prehistoric site that contains a feature or features such as a fire hearth,
post –hole mold, or pit
(m) Any historic site that has an unusual feature such as Civil War earthworks,
water-mill raceway, or slave quarters. etc.
(n) All sites that contain evidence of a Historic or Proto-Historic Indian tribe such
as Choctaw, Chickasaw, or Natchez ceramic sherds, gunflints, glass trade
beads, etc.
(o) Any prehistoric sites that contain unusual ceramic sherds or highly decorated
sherds (decorations other than Baytown Plain and Mulberry Creek Cord marked),
although a sample of these types will be saved due to Category A (representative
sample).
(p) All prehistoric sites that contain any of the following distinctive and unusual
artifacts and debitage.
1. Paleo-Indian Period tools and tool fragments
2. Early Archaic Period tools and tool fragments
3. Confirmed Middle Archaic tools and tool fragments
stone beads
ground stone
stone drills
stone needles
stone perforators
chipped quad-faces and tri-faces
Benton-Sykes-White Mountain points and knives
Eva-Morrow Mountain points and knives
Turkey Tail points and knives
St. Helena points and knives
St. Tammany points and knives
Tangipaoa-Evans points and knives
Point and knife types that are not found or rarely found in
Mississippi

2

4. Unusual lithic material
any stones that are green in color
Novaculite
Fort Payne chert
Obsidian
Any other lithic type that may have been carried a great distance
(other than water transported Citronell and Tuscaloosa gravels)
With the above-listed criteria, we believe that between 5 percent and 40
percent of the new sites in any given survey will be designated as significant.
This will be true unless the land area surveyed has undergone a great deal of
deflation due to erosion.
